    Active Warps Per Scheduler                                                        warp                           1,72
    Eligible Warps Per Scheduler                                                      warp                           0,06
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 19.3 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          1.72 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.06 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    smsp__issue_active.avg.per_cycle_active                                                                          0,05
    Avg. Active Threads Per Warp                                                                                    13,88
    Avg. Not Predicated Off Threads Per Warp                                                                        13,73
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 12.7 cycles being stalled waiting for an immediate constant cache  
          (IMC) miss. This represents about 38.3% of the total average of 33.2 cycles between issuing two               
          instructions. A read from constant memory costs one memory read from global memory only on a cache miss;      
          otherwise, it just costs one read from the constant cache. Immediate constants are encoded into the SASS      
          instruction as 'c[bank][offset]'. All threads access the same value.                                          
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 13.2 cycles being stalled waiting for a scoreboard dependency on a 
          L1TEX (local, global, surface, texture) operation. This represents about 39.6% of the total average of 33.2   
          cycles between issuing two instructions. To reduce the number of cycles waiting on L1TEX data accesses        
          verify the memory access patterns are optimal for the target architecture, attempt to increase cache hit      
          rates by increasing data locality or by changing the cache configuration, and consider moving frequently      
          used data to shared memory.                                                                                   
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   Instructions are executed in warps, which are groups of 32 threads. Optimal instruction throughput is         
          achieved if all 32 threads of a warp execute the same instruction. The chosen launch configuration, early     
          thread completion, and divergent flow control can significantly lower the number of active threads in a warp  
          per cycle. This kernel achieves an average of 13.9 threads being active per cycle. This is further reduced    
          to 13.7 threads per warp due to predication. The compiler may use predication to avoid an actual branch.      
          Instead, all instructions are scheduled, but a per-thread condition code or predicate controls which threads  
          execute the instructions. Try to avoid different execution paths within a warp when possible. In addition,    
          ensure your kernel makes use of Independent Thread Scheduling, which allows a warp to reconverge after a      
          data-dependent conditional block by explicitly calling __syncwarp().

    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 21.5 cycles being stalled waiting for an immediate constant cache  
          (IMC) miss. This represents about 42.3% of the total average of 50.8 cycles between issuing two               
          instructions. A read from constant memory costs one memory read from global memory only on a cache miss;      
          otherwise, it just costs one read from the constant cache. Immediate constants are encoded into the SASS      
          instruction as 'c[bank][offset]'. All threads access the same value.                                          
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 21.2 cycles being stalled waiting for a scoreboard dependency on a 
          L1TEX (local, global, surface, texture) operation. This represents about 41.7% of the total average of 50.8   
          cycles between issuing two instructions. To reduce the number of cycles waiting on L1TEX data accesses        
          verify the memory access patterns are optimal for the target architecture, attempt to increase cache hit      
          rates by increasing data locality or by changing the cache configuration, and consider moving frequently      
          used data to shared memory.                                                                                   
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   Instructions are executed in warps, which are groups of 32 threads. Optimal instruction throughput is         
          achieved if all 32 threads of a warp execute the same instruction. The chosen launch configuration, early     
          thread completion, and divergent flow control can significantly lower the number of active threads in a warp  
          per cycle. This kernel achieves an average of 19.9 threads being active per cycle. This is further reduced    
          to 19.8 threads per warp due to predication. The compiler may use predication to avoid an actual branch.      
          Instead, all instructions are scheduled, but a per-thread condition code or predicate controls which threads  
          execute the instructions. Try to avoid different execution paths within a warp when possible. In addition,    
          ensure your kernel makes use of Independent Thread Scheduling, which allows a warp to reconverge after a      
          data-dependent conditional block by explicitly calling __syncwarp().

    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 19.8 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          1.57 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.06 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 12.2 cycles being stalled waiting for an immediate constant cache  
          (IMC) miss. This represents about 39.1% of the total average of 31.1 cycles between issuing two               
          instructions. A read from constant memory costs one memory read from global memory only on a cache miss;      
          otherwise, it just costs one read from the constant cache. Immediate constants are encoded into the SASS      
          instruction as 'c[bank][offset]'. All threads access the same value.                                          
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 13.4 cycles being stalled waiting for a scoreboard dependency on a 
          L1TEX (local, global, surface, texture) operation. This represents about 43.0% of the total average of 31.1   
          cycles between issuing two instructions. To reduce the number of cycles waiting on L1TEX data accesses        
          verify the memory access patterns are optimal for the target architecture, attempt to increase cache hit      
          rates by increasing data locality or by changing the cache configuration, and consider moving frequently      
          used data to shared memory.                                                                                   
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   Instructions are executed in warps, which are groups of 32 threads. Optimal instruction throughput is         
          achieved if all 32 threads of a warp execute the same instruction. The chosen launch configuration, early     
          thread completion, and divergent flow control can significantly lower the number of active threads in a warp  
          per cycle. This kernel achieves an average of 13.1 threads being active per cycle. This is further reduced    
          to 13.0 threads per warp due to predication. The compiler may use predication to avoid an actual branch.      
          Instead, all instructions are scheduled, but a per-thread condition code or predicate controls which threads  
          execute the instructions. Try to avoid different execution paths within a warp when possible. In addition,    
          ensure your kernel makes use of Independent Thread Scheduling, which allows a warp to reconverge after a      
          data-dependent conditional block by explicitly calling __syncwarp().

    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 31.5 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          1.71 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.04 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 21.6 cycles being stalled waiting for an immediate constant cache  
          (IMC) miss. This represents about 40.1% of the total average of 53.9 cycles between issuing two               
          instructions. A read from constant memory costs one memory read from global memory only on a cache miss;      
          otherwise, it just costs one read from the constant cache. Immediate constants are encoded into the SASS      
          instruction as 'c[bank][offset]'. All threads access the same value.                                          
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 22.1 cycles being stalled waiting for a scoreboard dependency on a 
          L1TEX (local, global, surface, texture) operation. This represents about 40.9% of the total average of 53.9   
          cycles between issuing two instructions. To reduce the number of cycles waiting on L1TEX data accesses        
          verify the memory access patterns are optimal for the target architecture, attempt to increase cache hit      
          rates by increasing data locality or by changing the cache configuration, and consider moving frequently      
          used data to shared memory.                                                                                   
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   Instructions are executed in warps, which are groups of 32 threads. Optimal instruction throughput is         
          achieved if all 32 threads of a warp execute the same instruction. The chosen launch configuration, early     
          thread completion, and divergent flow control can significantly lower the number of active threads in a warp  
          per cycle. This kernel achieves an average of 19.7 threads being active per cycle. This is further reduced    
          to 19.6 threads per warp due to predication. The compiler may use predication to avoid an actual branch.      
          Instead, all instructions are scheduled, but a per-thread condition code or predicate controls which threads  
          execute the instructions. Try to avoid different execution paths within a warp when possible. In addition,    
          ensure your kernel makes use of Independent Thread Scheduling, which allows a warp to reconverge after a      
          data-dependent conditional block by explicitly calling __syncwarp().

    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 19.3 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          1.75 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.06 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 12.0 cycles being stalled waiting for an immediate constant cache  
          (IMC) miss. This represents about 35.6% of the total average of 33.8 cycles between issuing two               
          instructions. A read from constant memory costs one memory read from global memory only on a cache miss;      
          otherwise, it just costs one read from the constant cache. Immediate constants are encoded into the SASS      
          instruction as 'c[bank][offset]'. All threads access the same value.                                          
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 12.7 cycles being stalled waiting for a scoreboard dependency on a 
          L1TEX (local, global, surface, texture) operation. This represents about 37.6% of the total average of 33.8   
          cycles between issuing two instructions. To reduce the number of cycles waiting on L1TEX data accesses        
          verify the memory access patterns are optimal for the target architecture, attempt to increase cache hit      
          rates by increasing data locality or by changing the cache configuration, and consider moving frequently      
          used data to shared memory.                                                                                   
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   Instructions are executed in warps, which are groups of 32 threads. Optimal instruction throughput is         
          achieved if all 32 threads of a warp execute the same instruction. The chosen launch configuration, early     
          thread completion, and divergent flow control can significantly lower the number of active threads in a warp  
          per cycle. This kernel achieves an average of 12.4 threads being active per cycle. This is further reduced    
          to 12.3 threads per warp due to predication. The compiler may use predication to avoid an actual branch.      
          Instead, all instructions are scheduled, but a per-thread condition code or predicate controls which threads  
          execute the instructions. Try to avoid different execution paths within a warp when possible. In addition,    
          ensure your kernel makes use of Independent Thread Scheduling, which allows a warp to reconverge after a      
          data-dependent conditional block by explicitly calling __syncwarp().

    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 30.9 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          1.65 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.04 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 21.7 cycles being stalled waiting for an immediate constant cache  
          (IMC) miss. This represents about 42.5% of the total average of 50.9 cycles between issuing two               
          instructions. A read from constant memory costs one memory read from global memory only on a cache miss;      
          otherwise, it just costs one read from the constant cache. Immediate constants are encoded into the SASS      
          instruction as 'c[bank][offset]'. All threads access the same value.                                          
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 21.7 cycles being stalled waiting for a scoreboard dependency on a 
          L1TEX (local, global, surface, texture) operation. This represents about 42.6% of the total average of 50.9   
          cycles between issuing two instructions. To reduce the number of cycles waiting on L1TEX data accesses        
          verify the memory access patterns are optimal for the target architecture, attempt to increase cache hit      
          rates by increasing data locality or by changing the cache configuration, and consider moving frequently      
          used data to shared memory.                                                                                   
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   Instructions are executed in warps, which are groups of 32 threads. Optimal instruction throughput is         
          achieved if all 32 threads of a warp execute the same instruction. The chosen launch configuration, early     
          thread completion, and divergent flow control can significantly lower the number of active threads in a warp  
          per cycle. This kernel achieves an average of 19.4 threads being active per cycle. This is further reduced    
          to 19.4 threads per warp due to predication. The compiler may use predication to avoid an actual branch.      
          Instead, all instructions are scheduled, but a per-thread condition code or predicate controls which threads  
          execute the instructions. Try to avoid different execution paths within a warp when possible. In addition,    
          ensure your kernel makes use of Independent Thread Scheduling, which allows a warp to reconverge after a      
          data-dependent conditional block by explicitly calling __syncwarp().

    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 20.0 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          1.54 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.06 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 15.8 cycles being stalled waiting for an immediate constant cache  
          (IMC) miss. This represents about 51.6% of the total average of 30.7 cycles between issuing two               
          instructions. A read from constant memory costs one memory read from global memory only on a cache miss;      
          otherwise, it just costs one read from the constant cache. Immediate constants are encoded into the SASS      
          instruction as 'c[bank][offset]'. All threads access the same value.                                          
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 12.6 cycles being stalled waiting for a scoreboard dependency on a 
          L1TEX (local, global, surface, texture) operation. This represents about 41.0% of the total average of 30.7   
          cycles between issuing two instructions. To reduce the number of cycles waiting on L1TEX data accesses        
          verify the memory access patterns are optimal for the target architecture, attempt to increase cache hit      
          rates by increasing data locality or by changing the cache configuration, and consider moving frequently      
          used data to shared memory.                                                                                   
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   Instructions are executed in warps, which are groups of 32 threads. Optimal instruction throughput is         
          achieved if all 32 threads of a warp execute the same instruction. The chosen launch configuration, early     
          thread completion, and divergent flow control can significantly lower the number of active threads in a warp  
          per cycle. This kernel achieves an average of 11.6 threads being active per cycle. This is further reduced    
          to 11.6 threads per warp due to predication. The compiler may use predication to avoid an actual branch.      
          Instead, all instructions are scheduled, but a per-thread condition code or predicate controls which threads  
          execute the instructions. Try to avoid different execution paths within a warp when possible. In addition,    
          ensure your kernel makes use of Independent Thread Scheduling, which allows a warp to reconverge after a      
          data-dependent conditional block by explicitly calling __syncwarp().

    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 32.3 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          1.66 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.04 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 24.3 cycles being stalled waiting for an immediate constant cache  
          (IMC) miss. This represents about 45.3% of the total average of 53.7 cycles between issuing two               
          instructions. A read from constant memory costs one memory read from global memory only on a cache miss;      
          otherwise, it just costs one read from the constant cache. Immediate constants are encoded into the SASS      
          instruction as 'c[bank][offset]'. All threads access the same value.                                          
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 21.9 cycles being stalled waiting for a scoreboard dependency on a 
          L1TEX (local, global, surface, texture) operation. This represents about 40.7% of the total average of 53.7   
          cycles between issuing two instructions. To reduce the number of cycles waiting on L1TEX data accesses        
          verify the memory access patterns are optimal for the target architecture, attempt to increase cache hit      
          rates by increasing data locality or by changing the cache configuration, and consider moving frequently      
          used data to shared memory.                                                                                   
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   Instructions are executed in warps, which are groups of 32 threads. Optimal instruction throughput is         
          achieved if all 32 threads of a warp execute the same instruction. The chosen launch configuration, early     
          thread completion, and divergent flow control can significantly lower the number of active threads in a warp  
          per cycle. This kernel achieves an average of 21.9 threads being active per cycle. This is further reduced    
          to 21.9 threads per warp due to predication. The compiler may use predication to avoid an actual branch.      
          Instead, all instructions are scheduled, but a per-thread condition code or predicate controls which threads  
          execute the instructions. Try to avoid different execution paths within a warp when possible. In addition,    
          ensure your kernel makes use of Independent Thread Scheduling, which allows a warp to reconverge after a      
          data-dependent conditional block by explicitly calling __syncwarp().
